    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer5830350075550473284"><b>JESS MASTRIANI</b><br/> was dubbed "Lightning Girl" by the press when she developed a psychic ability to find missing children after she was struck by lightning during a huge storm. Now Jess has lost her miraculous powers...or at least she would like the media and the government to think so. All she wants is to be left alone. <br/> <br/> But it doesn't look like Jess is going to get her wish</span>
  <span id="freeText5830350075550473284" style="display:none"><b>JESS MASTRIANI</b><br /> was dubbed "Lightning Girl" by the press when she developed a psychic ability to find missing children after she was struck by lightning during a huge storm. Now Jess has lost her miraculous powers...or at least she would like the media and the government to think so. All she wants is to be left alone. <br /> <br /> But it doesn't look like Jess is going to get her wish -- especially not while working at a summer camp for musically gifted kids. When the father of a missing girl shows up to beg Jess to find his daughter, Jess can't say no. Now the Feds are on her tail again, as is one ornery stepdad, who'd like to see Lightning Girl...well, dead.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1093232836" />
    <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj"><img alt="Nasty Lady MJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506395877p2/4026143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1093232836?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasty Lady MJ" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj">Nasty Lady MJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1093232836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17175388755359262656">Coronovirus Reread: Somehow this book has not held well up to the test of time. The pop culture references feel super dated now and Jess is extremely immature. Of course, being twice her age now doesn't help matters-am I really that old, do not answer that. Anyway, I am taking a quick break from the series before I read the third book. I probably could shave off a star but I won't for now. <br/><br/>To see full binge review click <a href='http://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2014/11/07/jessica-you-do-know-google-locate-sort-of-made-you-obsolete-1800-where-r-you-series-by-meg-cabot/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here.</a><br/><br/>I could bitch and get really nit picky about some of the music things i</span>
  <span id="freeText17175388755359262656" style="display:none">Coronovirus Reread: Somehow this book has not held well up to the test of time. The pop culture references feel super dated now and Jess is extremely immature. Of course, being twice her age now doesn't help matters-am I really that old, do not answer that. Anyway, I am taking a quick break from the series before I read the third book. I probably could shave off a star but I won't for now. <br /><br />To see full binge review click <a href="http://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2014/11/07/jessica-you-do-know-google-locate-sort-of-made-you-obsolete-1800-where-r-you-series-by-meg-cabot/" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a><br /><br />I could bitch and get really nit picky about some of the music things in this book. And to be honest, I should. I really should. I don’t see how anyone can possibly get into a Musical Festival (Band Camp) or into the top chairs without being able to you know…read music. And it sort of contradicts the earlier book when Jess says that she bought some duets for her and Ruth to play (obviously, she could read music).<br /><br />Sigh, that aside. Though again fun book.<br /><br />This seems to be a disturbing pattern, huh? Book with lots and lots of faults but still fun.<br /><br />I think out of all the series though, this installment has one of the most clean cut plots. It’s a little predictable, but it comes together nicely. And I really loved the Jess and Rob moments in this one too. He’s in the book just enough, but not enough to completely overwhelm the plot.<br /><br />He’s probably, honestly, one of the least present Cabot male characters and I think that has an interesting effect on the books overall. I do wonder if the book had ran its intended run (eight books) if Rob would’ve been in the later installments more and how that would’ve effected it. For this book, I like his lack of presence. Oddly, it adds to the allure.<br /><br />There’s almost a third party love interests thrown in here, but the way Cabot handles the whole thing is good in the realistic type of way so bravo there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17175388755359262656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25337304-sarah?shelf=ya-novels">ya-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25337304-sarah?shelf=fantasy-real-world">fantasy-real-world</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1312883801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12794143367844783474">The second book in one of my favorite comfort series (do you guys have those? books that always cheer you up?). <br/><br/>Jess is back, working as a camp counselor with her best friend, Ruth. She is (unluckily) assigned to take care of the boys cabin after the guy who was supposed to take it bails out, and her old nemesis Karen Sue takes over her old cabin. <br/><br/>Honestly though? Thats the least of her problems. She is still dealing with the feds, who (accurately) don't believe that she lost her powers of being</span>
  <span id="freeText12794143367844783474" style="display:none">The second book in one of my favorite comfort series (do you guys have those? books that always cheer you up?). <br /><br />Jess is back, working as a camp counselor with her best friend, Ruth. She is (unluckily) assigned to take care of the boys cabin after the guy who was supposed to take it bails out, and her old nemesis Karen Sue takes over her old cabin. <br /><br />Honestly though? Thats the least of her problems. She is still dealing with the feds, who (accurately) don't believe that she lost her powers of being able to find people in her sleep. Her interactions with the 2 agents that are assigned to her always make me laugh- she is so sassy and doesn't really put up with any of their shit. She even brings them McDonald's when they are supposed to be surveilling her 'secretly'. <br /><br />Her interactions with the kids in her cabins are also great- she keeps them in line, doesn't let them get away with anything, but is still there for them and tries to be a fair counselor. <br /><br />As always, Rob, her love interest, makes me swoon. He is just such a good guy, trying to stay away from Jess because of his probation, but still driving 4 hours just to help her out. <br /><br />One of my favorite things in this book is that the code name the FBI assigned to Jess is 'Cassandra'-when I was younger I loved Greek mythology, and this is such a blatantly beautiful mythology reference. <br /><br />There are some things that bug me in this book- I don't always love Jess- she is quick to fight and acts pretty rash sometimes, but it just makes her character more complex and interesting. Meg Cabot write such real characters, and as always, I recommend her books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12794143367844783474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10569771185167504857" style="display:none">This book is a tenn book and is the sequel to When Lighting Strikes. By telling a reporter that she lost her physic abilities to find missing people, Jessica thought she got thr FBI off her back, but it just made them follow her everywhere. She still has secret packages from Roesmary (the person from 1-800-WHERERU that Jessica always tell the adresses of missing childrens to)about missing kids that wants to be found. Durung the camp, one of the conselors asked her if she could find his daughter for him. She was missing for a few weeks and was probably unwillingly taken away from her divorced mother and new stepfather. Accepting, Jessica calls Rob for a ride to find the daughter. When Rob came, they rescued the daughter and managed to get away saftly. But when they got back, they found out that one of the kids were missing and the FBI is also there. Jessica managed to find the kid in a cave after a vision, but inside the cave she had a encounter with the angry stepfather. When the stepfather was going to bash Jessica's head in with a flashlight, the kid came and and wacked him out with a rock. This story ended happily for everyone, but for Jessica because the FBI is following her around more intensly now that they are convinced Jessica's power was never gone. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5790743206927227528">Once again, it's Ruth's fault. That's how Jess explains her actions when she takes a summer job at Camp Wawasee as a counselor with Ruth. Jess somewhat tries to convince herself that 6 weeks away will do some good, for her and her family.<br/><br/>But it goes South almost immediately when she is reassigned to a boys cabin to cover a sick counselor. Now, she's in charge of 8 surely boys. Of course she finds the trouble maker instantly. Mullet boy, or Shane as she later finds out, is the king of all young j</span>
  <span id="freeText5790743206927227528" style="display:none">Once again, it's Ruth's fault. That's how Jess explains her actions when she takes a summer job at Camp Wawasee as a counselor with Ruth. Jess somewhat tries to convince herself that 6 weeks away will do some good, for her and her family.<br /><br />But it goes South almost immediately when she is reassigned to a boys cabin to cover a sick counselor. Now, she's in charge of 8 surely boys. Of course she finds the trouble maker instantly. Mullet boy, or Shane as she later finds out, is the king of all young jerks. She's constantly getting on to him for causing trouble and picking on small Lionel. (Lee-oh-nell)<br /><br />If dealing with Shane wasn't trouble enough, a distraught father begs Jess for her help in finding his daughter, Keely. Not having much of a choice once the picture is shoved under her nose, Jess finds her the next morning. However, Jess has learned her lesson and is determined to make sure Keely wants to be found.<br /><br />So guess who she call? Yep, Rob finally makes her appearance! Driving 4 hours just to pick her up, Rob and she make a trip and find Keely. It's clear up front that the care her mother is giving her is not sufficient. As Jess is trying to lead the girl to Rob's bike the crazy drunk step-father attacks them. Just escaping, Rob takes them to a McDonald's where she calls Keely's father.<br /><br />While waiting, Jess confronts the white van that has been following them. Our favorite Special Agents are back and determined to prove Jess lied and still has her powers.<br /><br />Going back to camp, Rob and Jess see multiple police and ambulances line the camp's front. Barging in, Jess learns Shane has drowned. Hitting Jess hard she is determined it isn't true, that he just ran off.<br /><br />Making things worst, Keely's mother's husband, Clay Larson, is after Jess and is potentially dangerous.<br /><br />Choosing not to care, she refuses to leave with Rob, risking their 'relationship' when he leaves angrily. Learning of Shane's whereabouts without going to sleep, it appears her powers are growing. Giving the feds the slip she, Ruth, and fellow counselors' Dave and Scott help her track him to some caves. Climbing in after Shane she finds him where he calls her out on being a liar about losing her powers. Claiming his stunt was to prove it.<br /><br />While down there, Mr. Larson traps them and attacks. Barely escaping, Shane and Jess are taken to the infirmary where she and Rob make up.<br /><br />Book ends with her and Ruth finally getting to relax on tubes in the river.</span>

<div id="review_161083225" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/161083225" />
    <a title="Karen Keyte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3164510-karen-keyte"><img alt="Karen Keyte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1263860035p2/3164510.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/161083225?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen Keyte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen Keyte" href="/user/show/3164510-karen-keyte">Karen Keyte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3164510-karen-keyte?shelf=teen-girls-adventure-mystery">teen-girls-adventure-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161083225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9743718927734104687">Jessica Mastriani, feisty heroine of When Lightning Strikes, is back and as cranky as ever in this second installment of the 1-800-Where-R-You series. After being struck by lightning during a freak April storm Jess developed a decidedly odd psychic power. If she looks at a picture of a missing person before she goes to bed, Jess wakes up knowing where that person is now. Exactly where he or she is. Every time. Unfortunately for Jess, having a freaky mutant power isn't all sunshine and roses. Esp</span>
  <span id="freeText9743718927734104687" style="display:none">Jessica Mastriani, feisty heroine of When Lightning Strikes, is back and as cranky as ever in this second installment of the 1-800-Where-R-You series. After being struck by lightning during a freak April storm Jess developed a decidedly odd psychic power. If she looks at a picture of a missing person before she goes to bed, Jess wakes up knowing where that person is now. Exactly where he or she is. Every time. Unfortunately for Jess, having a freaky mutant power isn't all sunshine and roses. Especially when the Feds, specifically the FBI and the U.S. Army, convinced her to let them 'study' her. One daring raid on a military base later (complete with a blown-up helicopter), Jess has decided that working with the Feds is not for her. She has informed all and sundry representatives of the U.S. government and the news media that her new-found psychic power has left as suddenly as it came and, even though the Feds obviously don't believe her, they've backed off a bit.<br /><br />All of which leaves Jess free to work as a counselor to a bunch of musical prodigies at Camp Wawasee. Jess figures a summer on a lake in northern Indiana is just what the doctor would order, you know, if the doctor knew she still had her freaky powers. A little sun, a lot of music, a cabin full of twelve-year-old girls eager to have their hair braided, what could go wrong? Alas, because Jess obviously has the worst luck in the world, the answer is 'everything.'<br /><br />First of all, a fellow counselor comes down with mono and Jess is asked to move in with a cabin full of twelve-year-old boys, no hair braiding skills required. They're paying her, so of course she's going to say yes, which means she's stuck with the eight little terrors. As if managing her pack of wild dogs, er.. boys, wasn't bad enough, a distraught father shows up at Wawasee and asks Jess to help him find his missing five-year-old daughter. Jess wants to help, but first she has to find a way to do that without giving away the fact that she still has her powers. This isn't going to be easy, but that's the story of Jess's life.<br /><br />Although this book is the series, enough back story is given so that a reader who picks this one up first isn't going to be lost. As with When Lightning Strikes, Code Name Cassandra is lifted above the mainstream of Y.A. fiction by Meg Cabot's stellar storytelling and the snappy dialogue. Lots of fun!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9743718927734104687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_884954447" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/884954447" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16718086-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559066080p2/16718086.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/884954447?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/16718086-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Alyssa by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/26491324-mina-rrat">Mina_rrat</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer884954447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16531750814146549602">So after reading the first of this series I immediately moved on to this book. Its hard to see think of a place where it stopped, it sort of became a blur. Still different from reading anything else. Again written as if you are reading Jess her diary, which is amusing and refreshing. Luckily there was less of Ruth in this book and Mike and Douglas weren't in it at all.<br/><br/>I was surprised about a few things, where did this camping counselor idea come from and how could she go away for 6 weeks, from R</span>
  <span id="freeText16531750814146549602" style="display:none">So after reading the first of this series I immediately moved on to this book. Its hard to see think of a place where it stopped, it sort of became a blur. Still different from reading anything else. Again written as if you are reading Jess her diary, which is amusing and refreshing. Luckily there was less of Ruth in this book and Mike and Douglas weren't in it at all.<br /><br />I was surprised about a few things, where did this camping counselor idea come from and how could she go away for 6 weeks, from ROB?? But I guess it fit well into the story. Otherwise there wouldn't have been a Dave or Scott to become friends with. Or a Shane to annoy the living crap out of her. She's not such a good camp counselor. I would get kicked out for the stuff she does with the kids.<br /><br />There were a few factors that started to annoy me even more though. Rob is being a pain in the ass. He keeps holding on the the stupid excuse for not getting together with Jessica, while he goes across the country for her. Ruth is being unbearably annoying and whiny. Most of the characters are stressing Jess about her gift not being gone, which of course is true, but they are forcing her to be that way. The feds keep taps on her and follow her around everywhere.<br /><br />I enjoyed reading it anyway, can't wait to start the next book. Thanks again Mia ;) I just need to know how things work out for Jess.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16531750814146549602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11424504321249380713">This was a fun little book. It was witty, quirky, and enjoyable. Took about 45 minutes to read. It read as though it was more of a lead in to the next book, as opposed to a standalone book, but this did not decrease the enjoyment of the book itself. It is a series that should not be read out of order, however.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1296573718052190433">2.5 to 3 stars. Cabot originally wrote this as Jenny Carroll, and with good reason - it's an edgier read with more grit than her Princess Diaries and Mediator series. Her heroine, Jess, cusses, spends a lot of time in detention, and just generally likes life a little close to the edge. Jess isn't a bad girl, but she has a few bad habits. The books are obviously geared toward teens who find the Princess books a little young and want their fiction a little spicier than the Mediator books. <br/><br/>I've rea</span>
  <span id="freeText1296573718052190433" style="display:none">2.5 to 3 stars. Cabot originally wrote this as Jenny Carroll, and with good reason - it's an edgier read with more grit than her Princess Diaries and Mediator series. Her heroine, Jess, cusses, spends a lot of time in detention, and just generally likes life a little close to the edge. Jess isn't a bad girl, but she has a few bad habits. The books are obviously geared toward teens who find the Princess books a little young and want their fiction a little spicier than the Mediator books. <br /><br />I've read both book 1 (When Lightning Strikes) and book 2 (this one) so far, and I by far liked book 1 best of the two, though neither one of them do much for me. Jess is likeable enough, but the books are pretty repetitive and Jess a little too hard-headed and slow on the uptake. I may read book 3 sometime in the future, but I need some time away from the 1-800 series first.</span>

<div id="review_3651796250" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3651796250" />
    <a title="Ken Finlay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/114976189-ken-finlay"><img alt="Ken Finlay" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3651796250?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ken Finlay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ken Finlay" href="/user/show/114976189-ken-finlay">Ken Finlay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3651796250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16666422621169879397">This is a very silly book and all the better for it.<br/>Jess, 16, was hit by lightning and ever since has been able to unerringly find missing people. But she has to pretend that she no longer has the ability in order to avoid being recruited by the FBI - they think she is lying and keep Jess under surveillance..<br/>In order to put off a summer spent working at her parents' restaurant she takes a job as a counsellor at a music camp for kids. Of course this means she is now 4 hours away from her 'boyfrie</span>
  <span id="freeText16666422621169879397" style="display:none">This is a very silly book and all the better for it.<br />Jess, 16, was hit by lightning and ever since has been able to unerringly find missing people. But she has to pretend that she no longer has the ability in order to avoid being recruited by the FBI - they think she is lying and keep Jess under surveillance..<br />In order to put off a summer spent working at her parents' restaurant she takes a job as a counsellor at a music camp for kids. Of course this means she is now 4 hours away from her 'boyfriend' Rob (well, he would be her boyfriend if it was Jess's decision and if he wasn't hung up about her being underage).<br />There she meets the obnoxious Shane, a child who plays music like a god but only wants to be a footballer.<br />While there is some finding to be done the best parts of the book are about her interaction with the kids, some of it is hilarious.<br />Every now and then you forget that Jess is a teenager, only to be reminded that at heart she's more aware than might appear at first.<br />It's an uplifting fast read - 3.5 Stars.<br />P.S. It was only after writing this review that I realised it was the second book in the series - I've since read book 1 and posted a review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16666422621169879397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3006987766" />
    <a title="Jamii" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30770782-jamii"><img alt="Jamii" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545459791p2/30770782.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamii" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamii" href="/user/show/30770782-jamii">Jamii</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30770782-jamii?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30770782-jamii?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30770782-jamii?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30770782-jamii?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30770782-jamii?shelf=empty-shelf-2019">empty-shelf-2019</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3006987766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6680384919407242576">Our quirky protagonist returns to cause more trouble in this book. Still being monitored by the feds, she heads off to be a counselor at an orchestra summer camp for six weeks. Secretly working with Rosemary the hotline receptionist to find missing children, while keeping up the facade that she’s lost her abilities. Somehow even at this distant private camp in the woods she winds up agreeing to help a man find his daughter. Inevitably trouble follows suit not just with the case but within the ca</span>
  <span id="freeText6680384919407242576" style="display:none">Our quirky protagonist returns to cause more trouble in this book. Still being monitored by the feds, she heads off to be a counselor at an orchestra summer camp for six weeks. Secretly working with Rosemary the hotline receptionist to find missing children, while keeping up the facade that she’s lost her abilities. Somehow even at this distant private camp in the woods she winds up agreeing to help a man find his daughter. Inevitably trouble follows suit not just with the case but within the camp as well. Again there were several obvious typos causing me to drop a star. However the characters and plots are well written, light hearted mostly and goofy. The image of the 16 year old girl causing so much mayhem is hysterical.</span>

<div id="review_3393157085" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer10066714530181070214">While I enjoyed the first, I loved this second book. This book is set in a camp. Even though I don't like camping... I do love campsites as a setting for books because there are so many possibilities for what could happen.   <span id="freeText10066714530181070214" style="display:none">While I enjoyed the first, I loved this second book. This book is set in a camp. Even though I don't like camping... I do love campsites as a setting for books because there are so many possibilities for what could happen. The characters were a lot stronger than they were in the first book and their personalities went further than 'bad boy' and 'fat girl' etc. Instead we had actual distinctive traits that defined them quite well. I don't own the next two books, unfortunately, but I plan on picking them up at some point and reading them. This is a gripping series.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9325148547055983979">So parts of it were really dated (some pop culture references that were way outdated) and there was one part where the main character describes her tanned skin as "like Pocahontas" that I thought was insensitive. It was a C+/B- book until that point, but I think I'll mark it down to a C the more I think about it. <br/>I<br/> much prefer some of her other books/series, but I still love Cabot's teen voice.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3395907097&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3395907097" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18215182229912723564">I give this 5 stars because when I first read it in 2005, I loved this book. It's quick, fun, and has a great premise. I wish Meg Cabot would rewrite it to meet today's standards- specifically the homophobic jokes, but there are more problematic tendencies through the series. The series has some great things...one just has to acknowledge that there are issues.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eppPzRyhLftc6XVBacCrpi7NSkc4Czut7K5p0UDZXMg3RlTaBM4hYQEe6IjlQTs5MvH73KhCGJlaFchNCKLlFw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('h3GGD+c8FafqihOtsbQw+Ei8QFVM/DcgW9MkyJC1AHTKrZ0Y/1MZPbd9jmQ9NaBnVIDxzty1FBTtaIVU2M65qw==')})
  }
